There are many different types of at-home composting systems available: ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä 1 - Tumblers - Compost tumblers are a common type of composting bin that allows the user to spin the compost bin, in order to aerate the compost pile. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä 2 - At-home compost solutions - Denver Urban Gardens has these wooden pallet made compost bins that allow the compost to naturally aerate. These can be moved to allow for the compost bin to be mixed. 3 - Vericomost - This type of composting system is great for people who live in apartments or have smaller backyards as it takes up less space. In vermicompost systems, worms are introduced, which break down the food and yard scraps quickly. The worms produce "castings" which are high in nutrients and can help fertilize your garden.

Why is composting important? üå± Even though food is decomposable, when it's buried in a landfill next to plastics and other nonbiodegradable materials, it can take decades or more for the food to degrade. üå± When food breaks down in the landfill, it generates about 20 times more carbon dioxide than it would if it were in a compost bin. üå± Carbon dioxide is a greenhouse gas that leads to global warming. üå± Adding food to the landfill takes up landfill space, which means more landfills will need to be built quicker.

This is a molded fiber product, but it can't be recycled because it has food residue on the container. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Composting sounds like a good option, but these items can be coated with substances that don't degrade fully and contaminate the compost. To prevent grease from soaking through, they are sprayed with different coatings such as plastic or PFAs (known as "forever chemicals"). ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä There's no way to tell the difference between coatings unless its labeled with a certification. If it is labeled with the word "Compostable" or has the BPI logo, that tells you its passed lab testing standards -- but not necessarily field testing. Many commercial composters will accept these items, but not all. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä The CMA certification is a new one that is based on field testing, and some facilities are moving to only accepting items that have this badge. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Whew! Compostable packaging can definitely be confusing! Our advice is to look for "compostable" on labels, check with your local facility, and when it doubt, throw it out! ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä @a1organics_co

Turtle Tip - Swapping out plastic grocery and produce bags for reusable bags made out of organic cotton or hemp is a simple way to reduce plastic use for food storage. Plastic bags are nearly impossible to recycle since these thin bags jam the recycling machinery at recycling centers. Opting for a reusable produce and grocery bag can eliminate hundreds of bags from entering the waste stream every year.üåé

Summer Sustainability Tip #4 ‚Äì Wanting to plant some new plants in your yard? If you live in an area suspectable to droughts, plant drought-tolerant plants to reduce the amount of water you use on gardening! This is especially important in the summer months when many states across the USA have brought warnings and some even have water limits. Did you know that, ‚ÄúThe average American family uses 320 gallons of water per day, about 30 percent of which is devoted to outdoor uses. More than half of that outdoor water is used for watering lawns and gardens.‚Äù (Source: Water Sense, An EPA Partnership Program)

Summer Sustainability Tip #3 ‚Äì Sun dry laundry rather than drying it in the dryer. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Sun drying laundry instead of drying it in the dryer can save energy on drying clothing. Summer Sustainability Tip #2 ‚Äì Participate in Meatless Monday to reduce greenhouse gas emissions released from factory farming.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Animal production is environmentally tolling in land use, water use, and greenhouse gases emitted from production. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä The ‚Äútotal emissions from global livestock: 7.1 Gigatonnes of Co2-equiv per year, representing 14.5 percent of all anthropogenic GHG emissions.‚Äù (Source: Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations)‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Additionally, it takes 616 gallons to produce just 4 ounces of hamburger beef (source: Water Education Foundation). By skipping eating meat just once a week, you can reduce hundreds of gallons of your food's water footprint and reduce food-related greenhouse gas emissions as well!‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Have a favorite vegetarian or vegan restaurant in your community? Summer Sustainability Tip #1 ‚Äì Turn up the air conditioner to save energy ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä One way to save energy and money in the summer is by turning up your air conditioner a few degrees so the air conditioner can run for shorter times. What are the macro-problem with microplastics? ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä One of the main issues associated with trashy dining is the release of microplastics from plastic waste left in the landfill or the ocean. These small particles of plastic are highly problematic for several reasons and are impossible to filter out at wastewater treatment plants. This has led to our water containing microplastics, with 90% of rainwater samples being contaminated, and plastic pollution spreading all around the planet ‚Äì even to remote areas.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Microplastics can also tie some other toxic or harmful compounds to themselves, which is alarming, since not only animals consume microplastics ‚Äì so do we. According to recent studies, an average human consumes one credit card worth of plastic every single week!

Trashy dining, when you receive single-use materials alongside your food, has a big impact on wildlife. üóëüèî‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Marine habitats are being flooded with tons of plastic. According to estimates, by the year 2050, there will be more plastic in the ocean than fish! Animals can then mistake all this litter for food or get entangled in it, leading to injury or even death. Often, when animals consume plastic, this can make them think that they are full even when they are dying of starvation.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Besides the danger it poses to animals, this litter is also ruining beautiful ecosystems, which are now covered in layers of trash.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Here at PlasticScore, we are on mission to bring an end to trashy dining and make sure that you can eat trash-free, no matter where you go.

Purchase non-perishable food items in glass or metal rather than plastic. For example, opt for the pasta sauce in a glass jar over a plastic container. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä 2. Purchase loose item produce rather than produce wrapped in plastic or grouped together in plastic mesh bags. For example, opt for buying single apples rather than a pack of apples stored in a thin plastic mesh bag. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä 3. If your store doesn't let you bring your own bags, try placing your items back in your cart after paying for them and bag your items in your car. Takeout Sustainability Tip - Reuse restaurant to-go packaging to extend the life of the packaging, when possible. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä @seekerofplaces ordered takeout from a local Denver restaurant and received her enchiladas in this aluminum packaging. Looking to make a refreshing summer drink without the waste? Sydney from the PlasticScore team made a zero waste watermelon drink that resulted in no waste and only a refreshing drink for Plastic Free July! ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Here's how to do it: 1. Cut half a watermelon into big chunks 2. Compost the watermelon skin 3. Put the chunks in a blender and blend until fully liquid 4. Optional - You can strain out the watermelon juice if you don't want extra pulp. This one is unstrained. 5. Add in some ice cubes - These ice cubes are made in a sustainable silicone container bought from @packagefreeshop 6. Cover the rest of the watermelon with a beeswax wrap - This kind is from @beeswrap 7. Enjoy!

Bring your own: Staying safe while dining out during COVID-19 | Tip #3 ‚Äì Reusable Straw‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä When restaurants start to reopen, we suggest bringing your own reusable straw rather than using the single-use straw at the restaurant. Even though the inside of the single-use straw is sanitary, the paper or plastic wrap packaging could be contaminated by anyone who handled it along it‚Äôs way to you.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä By bringing your own straws or cutlery to restaurants, you‚Äôre eliminating unnecessary contact with objects that could contain coronavirus, while reducing your own waste in the process.

Bring your own: Staying safe while dining out during COVID-19 | Tip #2 ‚Äì Reusable Cutlery‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä When restaurants start to reopen, many restaurants are likely to only offer single-use utensils instead of reusable cutlery. However, single-use items are not always more sanitary. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä For example, if a restaurant gives you a plastic cutlery set wrapped in plastic, the inside items are clean, but the outside wrapper could be contaminated from the server‚Äôs hands who gave the cutlery to you, or someone who handled it earlier on. When you open up the utensils, you touch the outside plastic wrapping which can contaminate your hands and then goes onto the utensils.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä We recommend bringing your own cutlery set when going to a restaurant. Win-Win-Win!

Tips to a Sustainable Thanksgiving - Leftovers ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Oftentimes, there are leftovers from Thanksgiving meals that folks enjoy the days following Thanksgiving. Planning on sharing the leftovers with your guests? Tips to a Sustainable Thanksgiving - Food, Part 2‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Purchase fresh fruits and vegetables from a local farmers market to cut down on food packaging and emissions from produce traveling long ways to arrive at your table. If farmers markets are not available in your area, try shopping for fresh fruits and vegetables that are sold without packaging. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Another tip is to only make the amount of food that you think you and your guests will eat. Food waste is a big environmental issue. During Thanksgiving alone, consumers end up throwing out nearly 200 million pounds of turkey (Source: Natural Resources Defense Council). If you plan on having turkey or another type of meat served for Thanksgiving, consider purchasing a smaller portion of meat, rather than the whole animal, to cut down on unnecessary food waste.
Nov 17, 2020, 1:02 PM
Tips to a Sustainable Thanksgiving - Food, Part 1‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Try adding in some vegetarian or vegan dishes to your meal. This will help cut down on CO2 and other emissions released from meat products.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä If possible, try shopping for food items that you need in the bulk section. If food items are not available in the bulk section, opt for items packaged in paper or aluminum, since these are much easier to recycle than plastic.

Sustainable Halloween Tip #2 - Save the Pumpkin Seeds! ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä In our last post, we talked about a way to reduce food waste from carving pumpkins is to save the seeds! ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Baking pumpkin seeds is pretty simple! You'll need pumpkin seeds, olive oil, and sea salt. Once you've cleaned your pumpkin seeds and removed the pumpkin "guts" you'll place them on a baking sheet and put olive oil and sea salt on top. Bake at 400 degrees for 5-10 minutes, or until the seeds are golden brown. Then you're ready to enjoy them, once they are cooled!‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä You can even put different flavors on top, such as paprika! Hey Denver Friends, TrashBlitz Denver is just a few days away! TrashBlitz Denver is a community-based project designed to engage Coloradans in measuring plastic pollution in the Denver area.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä TrashBlitz Denver will launch on October 25th, 2020 and will continue to October 31st, 2020. The goal of this event is to get Coloradans to go out to randomly generated, predetermined locations in Denver and collect data on plastic pollution (type, material, and brand) through the TrashBlitz Web App to help generate a relevant action plan for Colorado. The findings, which are designed to be open source, will help show a clear and immediate need to push for policy change that centers around source reduction. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä If you aren't comfortable going out for a cleanup, you can still contribute by doing an at home audit and gathering information about the items in your home you will throw away. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Sign up now to help Colorado reduce plastic pollution through the link in our bio!

A Look at the Issues with Plastic ‚Äì Plastics that are Better‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä We talked yesterday about how plastic No. 3, 6, and 7 are the hardest plastics to find recyclers for and are plastics to try to avoid. Plastic No. 1, 2, and 5 are plastics that are less toxic and are more feasible to recycle, as more recycling centers take back and can find buyers for this plastic.
Oct 19, 2020, 9:03 AM
A Look at the Issues with Plastic ‚Äì Plastics to Avoid ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Plastic No. 3, No. 6 & No. 7 are more toxic to make than other plastics and are much harder, if not impossible, to find a recycling market for. These plastics are typically destined for the landfill. Plastic No. 3 is PVC, plastic No. 6 is PS or Styrofoam and plastic No. 7 are other hard plastics, such as plastic water jugs. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Keep a look out for our next post, where we will talk about which plastic numbers are better than these.

A Look at the Issues with Plastic ‚Äì Recycling Pt. 4‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Did you know that plastic production is expected to double by 2040 and quadruple by 2050? As we highlighted in our last post, the manufacturers of plastics typically don‚Äôt buy back their plastic because the quality degrades so quickly. Therefore, new plastic must be made to keep up with the demand. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä This is different than manufactures of glass or metal products, who do buy back their products since these can be endlessly recyclable. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä We love how so many of you are doing your part to reduce plastic use in your life! A Look at the Issues with Plastic ‚Äì Recycling Pt. 3‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Unlike glass or metal, which can be endlessly recycled, plastic loses its quality when it is recycled. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä A plastic bottle cannot be infinity turned into a plastic water bottle forever. Once recycled, it will need to be downgraded and made into a less quality plastic product, such as carpeting or a t-shirt. This represents a linear cycle, where the plastic can be recycled a few times, until its properties have been fully utilized and the plastic gets sent to the landfill.

A Look at the Issues with Plastic ‚Äì Recycling Pt. 2‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Not all plastics can be recycled. For a plastic item to be recycled, there needs to be a market that will buy the plastic product. If there is no market, no manufactures will purchase the recycled plastic content, as often times it is cheaper to create products using virgin plastic.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Low-grade plastics, including chip bags or other soft plastics such as plastic wrap or snack pouches, do not have a market for recycling and cannot be recycled via curbside recycling due to economics of scale. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Do you recycle? A Look at the Issues with Plastic ‚Äì Recycling Pt. 1 ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Recycling is a great way to give plastics, and other products, another life. There are many different types of plastics, which are typically categorized by a number between 1-7. Some plastics are much easier to recycle then others. Due to this, in the USA, only 9% of the plastics that are produced are recycled. The other 91% of the plastics either end up in landfills, being burned, or littered into the environment. Likely more than 9% of plastics are placed into the recycling bin by consumers. However, either due to the contamination of recycling or not having buyers to buy pack the recycled content, only 9% of plastics are recycled.

A Look at the Issues with Plastic ‚Äì Downstream Problems Pt. 3‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä In 1862 the first plastic ever created was shown in London at the Great International Exhibition. Plastic creation has taken off since 1832, and in 1839 polystyrene, which is mainly used to create Styrofoam, was created. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä With plastics being around for a bit more than 180 years, the first plastics ever created, and all of those created since, still exist in our environment today in some way or another. Whether a new piece of plastic was recycled and turned into another product or larger plastics that break down into microplastics, every piece of plastic ever created still exists!

A Look at the Issues with Plastic ‚Äì Downstream Problems Pt. 1‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä When we compost food scraps, fruits, leaves, and newspapers all of these items are broken down naturally, creating nutrient-rich soil in the process. Everything that's compostable breaks down into soil, which allows new life to grow! ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä When looking at plastics, these materials can never fully biodegrade. Larger pieces of plastic can break down into smaller pieces of plastics, that eventually become microplastics. When plastics break down in the ocean, animals confuse these microplastics for food and eat the microplastic. This tricks the animal into thinking that they are full since their stomach is full of plastic, but they end up starving to death due to the lack of nutrients. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Do you know of some other downstream problems with plastics? A Look at the Issues with Plastic ‚Äì The problem with how plastics are made. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä In our last post, we talked about how plastic is made and derived from oil. With plastic being made from oil, there are many environmental impacts that are created from just producing the plastic pellets that will be turned into the various plastics that we utilize. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Extracting oil from the ground, especially over the open ocean, can cause water contamination when oil spills occur, which can lead to death for ocean animals.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä For oil that is extracted on the ground, this can impact local wildlife migration patterns or habitat due to the intense human activity around these drilling sites within natural spaces.

What is plastic made out of? Let‚Äôs take a look! ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä The basic components that make up plastic are derived mainly from oil in addition to natural gas and coal.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Oil is created through dead plants and animals decomposing and layers of sediment covering their remains over millions of years. The combination of heat and pressure turns these decomposed bodies into oil. From there, oil is pumped from the ground and sent to a refinery to refine the oil in different ways to create various products, including oil for driving cars or for making plastic.

Summer Sustainability Tip #7 ‚Äì Use reef safe sunscreen to protect natural aquatic habitats. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Opt for sunscreen that does not contain oxybenzone or octinoxate, which can be harmful to ocean animals and corals. Did you know that, ‚ÄúUp to 6,000 tons of sunscreen are estimated to wash into coral reefs around the globe each year. And as the National Park Service cautions, rather than being evenly distributed, much of that sunscreen is concentrated at popular diving, swimming, and snorkeling sites‚Äîsuch as national parks.‚Äù‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Why are concentrations of oxybenzone and octinoxate bad? ‚ÄúIn a 2016 study by Downs and colleagues from the National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration (NOAA) and other institutions, the authors found that baby coral exposed to oxybenzone and octinoxate exhibited signs of distress, including coral bleaching‚Äîa condition that leaves coral vulnerable to infection and prevents it from getting the nutrients it needs to survive‚Äîas well as DNA damage, and abnormalities in their growth and skeleton.‚Äù‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä (Source: CR Consumer Reports)‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä What is your favorite brand of reef-safe sunscreen? Let us know below so others can find out!

GreenPeace recently published the study, "Circular Claims Fall Flat: Comprehensive U.S. Survey of Plastics Recyclability." The study looked at "plastic product waste collection, sortation and reprocessing in the United States....to determine the legitimacy of ‚Äúrecyclable‚Äù claims and labels on consumer plastic products" (Source: GreenPeace). ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Here's some of the important key takeaways from the report: ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä "1. Only some PET #1 and HDPE #2 plastic bottles and‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä jugs can be legitimately labeled as recyclable in the‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä U.S. today.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä 2. Common plastic pollution items, including single use‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä plastic food service and convenience products, cannot‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä be legitimately claimed as recyclable in the U.S.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä 3. Plastics #3-7 have negligible-to-negative value and‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä are effectively a category of products that municipal‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä recycling programs may collect, but do not actually‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä recycle. Plastic #3-7 waste collected in municipal‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä systems across the country is being sent to landfills‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä or incinerated.‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä 4. Can plastic bags be recycled? The simple answer for a vast majority of people living in the USA is no, they can't be recycled. ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä "Less than 1 percent of the tens of billions of plastic bags used in the U.S. each year are recycled" (Source: The Intercept_). ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä If plastic bags can't easily be recycled, how can we stop the waste? One great option is to bring your own grocery bags and produce bags to the grocery store or whenever you go shopping. When ordering takeout, ask for no bag, when possible, or if you're picking up the food, see if the restaurant can put your food into your own reusable bag! ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä What other tips do you have to reduce the use of plastic bags?

We love seeing restaurants commit to using reusable packaging to reduce or eliminate waste altogether! Zuni Cafe in San Francisco has switched over to completely reusable containers for their takeout meals! ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä "Zuni Cafe, the groundbreaking Californian restaurant on Market Street, is switching out their takeout containers, and is moving to reusable packages, only. According to Zuni, they‚Äôre first restaurant in San Francisco to completely commit to reusable packaging, serving every order of their iconic roast chicken or bread salad in a stainless steel box or bowl" (Source: Eater). ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Zuni Cafe is working with Dispatch Goods to manage its reusable container program. "How it works: When you place an order at a participating restaurant, there might be an option to tick a box for reusable packaging, adding a fee of one or two bucks. At Zuni, however, it‚Äôs not optional, and it won‚Äôt be broken out as a separate fee, it‚Äôs simply rolled into the bill. Dispatch Goods provides the restaurant with the containers, which are stainless steel boxes and bowls with fitted silicone lids. Customers are responsible for returning those containers, either to the restaurant, a Dispatch Goods bin (which are dotted around town), or by contacting the company to arrange a curbside pickup. Dispatch Goods then cleans and returns them to the restaurant" (Source: Eater). ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä What other restaurants do you know that offer reusable takeout containers?‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä üì∏ @zunicafe

Sustainable Restaurant Resolution Tip 7 ‚Äì Reuse packaging waste ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Sometimes, even with our best intentions, we still receive packaging waste in our takeout orders. Depending on the items you received, see if there might be a way to reuse some of these items. Some examples that our PlasticScore users have shared with us includes, using plastics bags until unusable and then making yarn out of the plastic bags to create your own heavy-duty bag. Other suggestions include using a tin to go container to store compostable seed start containers in and water the seed starts from the container. The possibilities are endless and allows the packaging to have another life before being disposed of.
Jan 14, 2021, 10:03 AM
Sustainable Restaurant Resolution Tip 6 ‚Äì Condiments ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Condiments definitely can make a meal take great, but oftentimes these are packaged in plastic containers or packets, which are typically hard or impossible to recycle. When ordering, make sure you specify what type of condiments you want and how many you would like. That way, you only end up with the condiments you know you‚Äôre going to use! ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä If you received too many condiments in a takeout order, consider saving the condiments for future to-go orders or even home cooked meals. This ensures that the condiments are being used, instead of going to the landfill unopened.
Jan 13, 2021, 1:01 PM
Sustainable Restaurant Resolution Tip 5 ‚Äì Ask for no napkins‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä ‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä‚†Ä Asking for no napkins is a great way to reduce waste, especially if your ordering takeout and can use reusable napkins that you have at home!
